[2026-04-04] Topic: Asana cleanup + Amazon writing standards upgrade | Actions: Archived 37 completed tasks in Asana (moved to Archive section). Our articles are formatted like reference cards (bullets, tables, fragments). Amazon docs are narrative-driven prose with embedded data. The rubric now enforces: max 30% bullet content, tables must have "so what" interpretation, prose is default, and formatting cannot substitute for writing. This will cause most existing articles to score lower on Economy — which is correct. The articles need rewriting, not reformatting.

[2026-04-04] Topic: Blind test 2 with genuinely different evaluators | Actions: Ran Evaluator A (strict Amazon writing rubric — bullet abuse, table abuse, formatting-as-content, 18-20 word sentences, purpose-first) and Evaluator B (subjective Brandon/Kate reader simulation — first paragraph test, shareability, actionability, signal-to-noise, voice). [2026-04-06] Topic: PS Forecast Tracker Dive v17 — justification reorder, calibration by horizon, Dive edit pattern discovered | Actions: Updated dive_forecast_calibration view to group by horizon (weekly/monthly/quarterly/year_end scored separately); moved Justification section above Full Year Projection table using SQL REPLACE on existing content via temp table; added all narrative sections (revisions/monthly/quarterly/year_end) to justification block; calibration table now shows horizon in parentheses. Diagnosed root cause: populate_forecast_tracker.py uses OLS trend + seasonal lookup (proj_seg), not the actual BayesianProjector class which properly builds priors and updates posteriors with recent evidence | Decisions: Current script is mislabeled — it's OLS, not Bayesian. [2026-04-09] Topic: PS Forecast Tracker — rewired populate_forecast_tracker.py to use BayesianProjector | Actions: Rewrote populate_forecast_tracker.py to use BayesianProjector.project_market() (proper Bayesian with ps.seasonal_priors, ie%CCP, calibration) instead of inline OLS; fixed import path (relative imports via prediction package); suppressed verbose cross-validation logging; ran successfully for all 10 markets + WW/EU5 aggregates — 1,656 rows, 0 missing; AU W15 now predicts 313 (was 77 with OLS), properly anchored to recent actuals | Decisions: BayesianProjector is the correct engine — recent evidence dominates via update_posterior(), seasonal priors from ps.seasonal_priors dampen one-time events, calibration factor from ps.calibration_state adjusts CI width. Script takes ~7min due to per-week DB queries but runs to completion. Year-end CIs very wide from quadrature compounding — acceptable for now.

[2026-04-09] Topic: PS Forecast Tracker — prediction quality audit after BayesianProjector run | Actions: Compared actuals vs predicted across all markets for weekly/monthly/quarterly registrations and cost; weekly predictions are solid (CA 9.5%, EU5 7.4%, WW 8.4% avg error; CI hit rates 79-100%); monthly predictions are broken — project_market_monthly() produces values 10-50x too high (AU Jan: 48,595 predicted vs 1,135 actual = 4,182% error); quarterly inherits the monthly bug | Decisions: Weekly BayesianProjector output is trustworthy and should be the anchor; monthly predictions should be derived from summing weekly predictions (not from project_market_monthly which has a fundamental scaling bug); cost CIs too tight for individual markets (need wider ±15% → ±25%).

[2026-04-09] Topic: PS Forecast Tracker — systemic prediction bias diagnosis | Actions: Analyzed per-week bias across all 14 actual weeks for all markets; checked seasonal_priors for W14/W15; confirmed bias is systemic not week-specific — US/UK/MX under-predict every single week (US: 0 over, 14 under, -5% to -33%), ES/AU/FR over-predict every week (ES: 14 over, 0 under, +6% to +63%); checked seasonal_index values (MX W15=0.54 compounds the issue but isn't the cause) | Decisions: Root cause is BayesianCore.update_posterior() prior-to-posterior weighting — 2025 historical mean dominates over 2026 evidence. The 60/40 trend blend and conjugate update aren't shifting enough toward recent run rate. Fix is either increasing evidence weight in posterior update or using shorter history window for prior. Seasonal priors make it worse for already-biased markets but aren't the primary driver.

[2026-04-09] Topic: PS Forecast Tracker — fixed systemic bias via prior weight cap reduction | Actions: Changed BayesianCore.update_posterior() prior_weight cap from 8→4 in core.py (50/50 prior/evidence split instead of 67/33); re-ran populate_forecast_tracker.py for all markets; re-derived monthly/quarterly/year-end from weekly sums | Decisions: Bias cut roughly in half — US went from -15.7% to -5.3%, UK -16.3% to -4.5%, WW -7.2% to -0.5% (near-perfect), AU +21.9% to +7.6%; avg absolute error improved across most markets (US 15.7%→8.0%, AU 22.3%→11.2%); remaining bias in ES/FR (over-predicting) and US/JP W15 (seasonal priors still pulling down) is seasonal_priors data quality, not core algorithm. W14→W15 transitions more reasonable (MX -19%→+6%, US -30%→-22%).

[2026-04-14] Topic: Why US/MX predicted regs declining — forecast revision history analysis | Actions: Queried ps.forecasts revision history for US/MX (W1-W17); queried US seasonal_priors W1-W17.
